                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, M, Msb, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَسْلِيمٌ</foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (God) <hi rend="ital">made him to be safe, secure,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free; saved, secured,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">freed, him;</hi> (M, Msb, TA;) <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الآفَاتِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from evils of any kind</hi>], (S, Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الآفَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from evil of any kind</hi>], (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الأَمْرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from the affair</hi>]. (M.) [Freytag assigns the same meaning to   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-1" target="اسلمهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> also, as on the authority of the Ham; in which I find no explanation of this verb except one which will be found later in this paragraph.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">التَّسْلِيمُ</foreign> is also <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">السَّلَامُ</foreign>, (S, K, TA,) as meaning <hi rend="ital">The saluting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">greeting,</hi> one <hi rend="ital">with a prayer for</hi> his <hi rend="ital">safety,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">security,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">freedom, from evils of any kind in</hi> his <hi rend="ital">religion and in</hi> his <hi rend="ital">person;</hi> and the interpretation thereof is [<hi rend="ital">the expressing a desire for</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">التَّخْلِيصٌ</foreign>; (Mbr, TA;) or <hi rend="ital">the saluting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">greeting,</hi> one <hi rend="ital">with a prayer for</hi> his <hi rend="ital">life;</hi> or, <hi rend="ital">by saying</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكَ</foreign> [q. v. infrà, voce <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ</foreign>]; syn. <foreign lang="ar">التَّحِيَّةُ</foreign>. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">He so saluted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">greeted, him</hi>]. (M, Msb.) [This, when said of God, virtually means <foreign lang="ar">سَلَّمَهُ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">He saved him;</hi> and should be rendered agreeably with this explanation in the phrase commonly used after the mention of the Prophet, <foreign lang="ar">صَلَّى ٱللّٰهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">May God bless and save him.</hi> You say also, <foreign lang="ar">سَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِالخِلَافَةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He saluted him with the acknowledgment of his being Khaleefeh;</hi> saying, <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَمِيرَ المُؤْمِنِينَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Salutation to thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">peace be on thee,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">O Prince of the Faithful.</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">التَّسْلِيمَةُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">The salutation that is pronounced on finishing every two rek'ahs in prayer:</hi> (Har p. 180:) [and also <hi rend="ital">that which is pronounced after the last rek'ah of each of the prayers</hi> (i. e. after the sunneh prayers and the fard alike), addressed to the two guardian and recording angels: (see my “ Modern Egyptians, ” ch. iii., p. 78 of the 5th ed.:) and <foreign lang="ar">سَلَّمَ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">He pronounced either of those salutations.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence also,] <foreign lang="ar">سلّم إِلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشَّىْءَ</foreign>, (S, K, *) inf. n. as above; (K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-2" target="اسلم" n="2" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> اليه الشىءَ</foreign>; (M;) <hi rend="ital">He gave to him the thing;</hi> (S, * M, K;) or <hi rend="ital">delivered it to him:</hi> (M:) [<hi rend="ital">he resigned it to him:</hi>] and <foreign lang="ar">سلّم إِلَيْهِ الوَدِيعَةَ</foreign>, (Mgh,) or <foreign lang="ar">سلّم الوَدِيعَةَ لِصَاحِبِهَا</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He delivered the deposit</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to him,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">to its owner:</hi> (Msb:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-3" target="اسلم" n="3" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> الثَّوْبَ إِلَى الخَيَّاطِ</foreign> (Mgh) signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">سلّمهُ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">He delivered the garment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">piece of cloth, to the tailor</hi>]. (Har p. 166.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  See also 4, in two places.          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  You say also, <foreign lang="ar">سلّم</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَجِيرُ نَفْسَهُ لِلْمُسْتَأْجِرِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The hired man gave himself up,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gave authority over himself, to the hirer.</hi> (Msb.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-4" target="أَسْلَمْتُهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَلَّمْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I left him in the power of him who desired to kill him</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to wound him.</hi> (Ham p. 115.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-5" target="اسلمهُ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لِلْهَلَكَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He gave him up to destruction</hi>]: in this case with [the prep.] <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> only. (Har p. 166.) And <pb n="1413"/><foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-6" target="اسلم" n="6" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>الرَّجُلَ</foreign>, (S, * M, Msb, *) or <foreign lang="ar">العَدُوَّ</foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">He left, forsook,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">deserted,</hi> (M, K,) <hi rend="ital">the man,</hi> (S, * M, Msb, *) or <hi rend="ital">the enemy;</hi> (K;) or <hi rend="ital">abstained from aiding,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">assisting, him;</hi> (S, M, Msb, K;) and <hi rend="ital">threw him into destruction.</hi> (IAth, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-7" target="اسلمهُ" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لِمَا بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He left him</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to that</hi> bane <hi rend="ital">which was in him:</hi> app. referring to the bite of a serpent, or any evil affection: see <foreign lang="ar">سَلِيمٌ</foreign>, third sentence]. (S, * M.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">سلّم أَمْرَهُ إِلَى ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20530-8" target="اسلمهُ" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, both meaning the same, (S, Msb, K, TA,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">He committed his case to God.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">سلّم الدَّعْوَى</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He acknowledged the truth</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">justice</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of the claim, demand,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suit;</hi> [<hi rend="ital">he conceded its truth</hi> or <hi rend="ital">justice;</hi>] from <foreign lang="ar">سلّم الوَدِيعَةَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لِصَاحِبِهَا</foreign>, expl. above; denoting an ideal delivering [or yielding of a thing to another person]. (Msb.) [Hence one says, <foreign lang="ar">سلّم أَنَّهُ كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He conceded that it was thus.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">التَّسْلِيمُ</foreign> signifies also [<hi rend="ital">The assenting,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">the giving</hi> [one's] <hi rend="ital">approval</hi> (S, K, TA) <hi rend="ital">unreservedly,</hi> (S,) to that which is ordained, or decreed, (S, K, TA,) by God; and <hi rend="ital">the submitting</hi> to his commands; and <hi rend="ital">the abstaining from offering opposition in the case in which it is not becoming</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to do so</hi>]. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">سلّم لِأَمْرِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He assented to the command of God:</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">he gave his approval to it:</hi>] or <hi rend="ital">he submitted to it;</hi> as also

                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">سَلَمَ</orth>
                  </form>,] inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامَةٌ</foreign> (S, M, A, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ</foreign> (A, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">سَلَمٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَلْمٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سِلْمٌ</foreign>, (Bd in xxxix. 30,) <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, safe,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">secure;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he escaped;</hi> (M, TA;) or <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, free;</hi> (TA;) <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الآفَاتِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from evils of any kind</hi>], (S, Mgh,) or <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الآفَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from evil of any kind</hi>], (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ البَلَآءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from trial,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affliction</hi>], (A, TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الأَمْرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from the affair</hi>]: (M:) <hi rend="ital">he</hi> (a traveller) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, safe, secure,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free, from evils of any kind:</hi> (Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar">سَلِمَ مِنَ العَيْبِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, free from fault, defect, imperfection, blemish,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vice;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">بَرِئَ</foreign>. (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">برأ</foreign>.) [Hence,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">لَا بِذِى تَسْلَمُ مَا كَانَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">گَذَا وَكَذَا</foreign>, (ISk, S, K, *) meaning <hi rend="ital">No, by God</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">Him</hi>] <hi rend="ital">who maketh thee to be in safety,</hi> (ISk, S, K,) [<hi rend="ital">such and such things were not;</hi>] and to two persons <foreign lang="ar">لا بذى تَسْلَمَانِ</foreign>, and to a pl. number <foreign lang="ar">لا بذى تَسْلَمُونَ</foreign>, and to a female <foreign lang="ar">لا بذى تَسْلَمِينَ</foreign>, and to a pl. number [of females] <foreign lang="ar">لا بذى تَسْلَمْنَ</foreign>. (ISk, S, K. *) And <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَفْعَلُ ذٰلِكَ بِذِى تَسْلَمُ</foreign>, meaning, <foreign lang="ar">بِذِى سَلَامَتِكِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I will not do that, by the Author</hi> (lit. <hi rend="ital">Lord</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Master</hi>) <hi rend="ital">of thy safety</hi>]; and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">بذى تَسْلَمَانِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">بذى تَسْلَمُونَ</foreign>. (Sb, M. [See also <foreign lang="ar">ذو</foreign>.]) And <foreign lang="ar">اِذْهَبْ بِذِى تَسْلَمُ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">اِذْهَبْ بِسَلَامَتِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Go thou with thy safety;</hi> or, <hi rend="ital">with the Author of thy safety</hi> to protect thee; meaning <hi rend="ital">go thou in safety</hi>]; and [to two persons] <foreign lang="ar">اِذْهَبَا بِذِى تَسْلَمَانِ</foreign>. (S, K.) <foreign lang="ar">ذى</foreign> is thus prefixed to a verb [as virtually governing it in the gen. case] like as <foreign lang="ar">آيَة</foreign> is in an instance mentioned under this latter word; but these are two extr. instances; for only a noun significant of time is [regularly] prefixed to a verb, as in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا يَوْمُ يُفْعَلُ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">يُفْعَلُ فِيهِ</foreign>: (Akh, S:) it is not prefixed to any but this verb <foreign lang="ar">تَسْلَمُ</foreign> [and its variations as above mentioned]. (Sb, M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And hence, (Mgh,) one says also, <foreign lang="ar">سَلِمَتْ لَهُ الضَّيْعَةُ</foreign>, meaning [<hi rend="ital">The landed estate</hi>] <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, free from participation to him;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">خَلَصَت</foreign>.                   </form> see 2, in nine places. [The first of the meanings there assigned to this verb is, in my opinion, more than doubtful. In all its senses, it seems to be properly trans.: when it is used as an intrans. verb, an objective complement is app. understood. Thus,] <foreign lang="ar">أَسْلَمَ</foreign> is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">أَسْلَفَ</foreign> [as meaning <hi rend="ital">He paid in advance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beforehand</hi>]; (S, M, Mgh, Msb;) <foreign lang="ar">الثَّمَنَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the price</hi>] being suppressed, though sometimes it is expressed; (Mgh;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20531-3-1" target="سلّم" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20529"/></foreign>; (M;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20531-3-2" target="تسلّم" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20529"/></foreign>, as occurring in a trad., where it is said, <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ تَسَلَّمَ فِى شَىْءٍ فَلَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَصْرِفُهُ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Whoso pays in advance for a thing, he shall not turn it over,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">transfer it, to another than him</hi>]; but Kt says that he had not heard this verb thus used except in this instance. (TA.) So the first of these verbs signifies in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">اسلم فِى الطَّعَامِ</foreign> (S) or <foreign lang="ar">فى البُرِّ</foreign> (Mgh) [<hi rend="ital">He paid in advance for the wheat</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">فى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشَّىْءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">for the thing</hi>], as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20531-3-3" target="سلّم" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20529"/></foreign>. (M.) And hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا أَسْلَمَ صُوفًا فِى لِبْدٍ أَوْ شَعَرًا فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِسْحٍ لَمْ يَجُزْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">If he give in advance wool for felt, or goats' hair for a garment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">piece, of haircloth, it will not be allowable</hi>]. (Mgh.) And so in the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">أَسْلَمْتُ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I paid in advance to him</hi>]. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also [<hi rend="ital">He resigned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">submitted, himself;</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسَهُ</foreign> being understood: or] <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, resigned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">submissive;</hi> (M, K;) and so

(M.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  One says also, <foreign lang="ar">أَسْلَمْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَنْهُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I left it</hi> [app. an affair, as in an explanation in the TK,] <hi rend="ital">after I had been</hi> [<hi rend="ital">engaged</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in it.</hi> (Ibn-Buzurj, K.)                   <foreign lang="ar">أَسْلَمَ</foreign>, meaning [<hi rend="ital">He was a pastor of sheep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goats; then</hi>] <hi rend="ital">he left them.</hi> (M.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [Freytag assigns to <foreign lang="ar">اسلم</foreign> another signification “ <hi rend="ital">Adscendere fecit</hi> (vid. a <foreign lang="ar">سُلَّم</foreign>), ” as from the Ham, p. 39: but this is app. a mistake, into which he has been led by a saying, there cited, of Zuheyr, which I read thus: <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">هَوِىَّ الدَّلْوِ أَسْلَمَهَا الرِّشَآءُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> (meaning, <hi rend="ital">The descent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">as the descent, of the bucket that the well-rope has let go</hi>): and by its being there said that “ you should not prefer any reading of <foreign lang="ar">هوى</foreign> to that with damm, though it has been said otherwise: ” whereas the correct reading is, in my opinion, <foreign lang="ar">هَوِىّ</foreign>, agreeably with what here follows:] Er-Riyáshee says, on the authority of AZ, that <foreign lang="ar">الهَوِىُّ</foreign>, with fet-h, is downwards; and with damm, upwards; and he cites the saying above as an ex. of the word as meaning downwards.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20546-2" target="سَلَمٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20538"/></foreign>, (S, [so in one of my copies, but omitted in the other copy,]) and signifies <hi rend="ital">Safety, security, immunity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">freedom, from faults, defects, imperfections, blemishes,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vices,</hi> (S, * [mentioned in one only of my two copies, and there as relating peculiarly to the third word,] K, [in which it ostensibly relates peculiarly to the first word, but in the CK, by the omission of a <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> before it, it is made to relate only to the second word,] and TA, [accord. to which it relates to the first and second words, as it is well known to do,]) <hi rend="ital">and from evils of any kind:</hi> (TA:) or [simply] <hi rend="ital">safety, security, immunity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">freedom;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20546-3" target="سَلَامَةٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20549"/></foreign>: (Sb, M:) IKt says that these two words may be dial. vars. [syn. each with the other]; or the former may be pl. of the latter [or rather a coll. gen. n. of which the latter is the n. un.]: (M, TA:) and Suh says, in the R, that most of the lexicologists hold them to have one [and the same] meaning: but that if they considered the language of the Arabs, and the distinction, or limitation, denoted by the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, they would see that between them is a great difference [inasmuch as the former has a large range of meaning which the latter has not, as will be seen from what follows]. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ</foreign> is an announcement of the continuance of <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامَة</foreign> [or safety, &amp;c.]: (Bd in xiii. 24:) [it may therefore be rendered <hi rend="ital">Safety,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">light and abide, on you;</hi> or, generally, <hi rend="ital">peace be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">light and abide, on you;</hi> for] it means <hi rend="ital">nothing disliked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil, shall befall you henceforth:</hi> (Bd in xvi. 34:) and <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكَ</foreign> [may be rendered in like manner; for it virtually] means <hi rend="ital">I will not do to thee anything that is disliked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil;</hi> (Bd and Jel in xix. 48;) <hi rend="ital">nor say to thee henceforward what would annoy thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">be disagreeable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil, to thee.</hi> (Bd ibid.) It may also be [rendered <hi rend="ital">May safety,</hi> &amp;c., or <hi rend="ital">peace, be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">light and abide, on you;</hi> as] a prayer for <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامَة</foreign>, to those to whom it is addressed, from the state in which they are at the time. (Bd in xxviii. 55.) [It is generally held that this salutation may not be used by, nor to, any but a Muslim.] In the beginning of an epistle, the approved practice is to write <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign>, without the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>; and in repeating it, at the end, to write it with that article. (Durrat el-Ghowwás, in De Sacy's Anthol. Gramm. Arabe, p. 72 of the Arabic text. [In the latter case, the general practice in the present day is to write simply <foreign lang="ar">وَالسَّلَام</foreign>, suppressing <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign>.]) In saluting the dead, one puts <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign> first, saying, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ سَلَامُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>. (Ham p. 367.) You also say, <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n20546-4" target="بِسَلَامَتِكَ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>مَا كَانَ كَذَا وَكَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">No, by thy safety, such and such things were not</hi>]. (S.) <foreign lang="ar">السُّلَامُ</foreign> is also a name of <hi rend="ital">God,</hi> (S, M, Msb, K,) [applied to Him in the Kur lix. 23, accord. to some for <foreign lang="ar">ذُو السَّلَامِ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">ذُو السَّلَامَةِ</foreign>,] because of his safety, or freedom, from defect, and imperfection, and cessation of existence; (IKt, M, TA;) or from variations, and as being the everlasting, who brings the creation to nought and will not come to nought; or, accord. to Suh in the R, He is so named [as being <hi rend="ital">the Author of Safety, Security,</hi> &amp;c.; i. e.] because He has rendered all his creatures safe, or free, from defectiveness, or unsoundness, and mankind and the jinn, or genii, from the betiding of injustice, or wrong, to them, from Him; and the expositors who assert that He is thus named because of his safety, or freedom, from imperfections, and evils of any kind, utter an unseemly saying, making <foreign lang="ar">سَلَامٌ</foreign> to be syn. with   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20546-5" target="سَالِمٌ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20554"/></foreign>, which latter applies only to him who is liable to evil of any kind, and who expects it, and then becomes safe, or free, from it. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">دَارُ السَّلَامِ</foreign> is an appellation of <hi rend="ital">Paradise,</hi> (M, K,) [applied thereto in the Kur vi. 127 and x. 26,] as being <hi rend="ital">the abode of everlasting safety,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">security;</hi> (Zj, M, TA;) <hi rend="ital">the abode of safety,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">security, from evils of any kind, from death and decrepitude and diseases</hi> [<hi rend="ital">&amp;c.</hi>]: (TA:) or as being <hi rend="ital">the abode of God.</hi> (M, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">سِلْمٌ</foreign>, in four places.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [As is there stated,] it signifies also <hi rend="ital">Salutation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">greeting;</hi> (M, TA;) particularly the <hi rend="ital">salutation of</hi>

                  <hi rend="ital">A ladder,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a series of stairs</hi> or <hi rend="ital">steps,</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">مِرْقَاةٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">دَرَجَةٌ</foreign>, (M,) or <foreign lang="ar">مِعْرَاجٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">upon which one ascends;</hi> (S, Mgh;) either <hi rend="ital">of wood</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of clay</hi> [<hi rend="ital">&amp;c.</hi>]: (Mgh:) said by Zj to be so called because it delivers thee (<foreign lang="ar">يُسَلِّمُكَ</foreign>) to the place to which thou desirest to go, (Mgh, TA,) i. e., to some high place, and thou hopest for safety (<foreign lang="ar">السَّلَامَة</foreign>) by means of it: (Er-Rághib, TA:) masc. and fem.; (Lth, M, Mgh;) [app., accord. to Lth and F, generally fem.; for] accord. to Lth, one says, <foreign lang="ar">هِىَ السُّلَّمُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ السُّلَّمُ</foreign>; (Mgh;) [and F says,] it is sometimes made masc.: (K:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">سَلَالِيمُ</foreign> (S, Mgh, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سَلَالِمُ</foreign>, (K,) [which latter is the original, for] the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">سَلَالِيمُ</foreign> is added by poetic license. (M, TA.) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">السُّلَّمُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Certain stars, below</hi> [<hi rend="ital">those called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">العَانَةُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">on the right of them;</hi> (K;) as being likened to the <foreign lang="ar">سُلَّم</foreign> [above-mentioned].                      <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَجِلْدَةُ بَيْنَ العَيْنِ وَالأَنْفِ سَالِمُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> (TA,) is futile: (K:) for, as IB says, Sálim was the son of Ibn-'Omar, who, by reason of his love of him, thus makes him to be as the skin between his eyes and his nose: or, as MF says, the truth is, that the said verse is by Zuheyr, and Ibn-'Omar used it as a proverb: and [SM says], if this be correct, it strengthens the saying of J.
